             <a href="/wiki/New_Covenant" title="New Covenant">
              New Covenant
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg" title="Christian cross">
         <img alt="Christian cross" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="400" height="18" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/20px-P_christianity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/30px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/40px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Portal:Christianity" title="Portal:Christianity">
         Christianity portal
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Christianity" title="Template:Christianity">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Christianity" title="Template talk:Christianity">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Christianity&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </b>
      (the
      <b>
       LDS Church
      </b>
      or, informally, the
      <b>
       Mormon Church
      </b>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Restorationism" title="Restorationism">
       restorationist
      </a>
      church that is considered by its followers to be the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restoration_(Latter_Day_Saint)" title="Restoration (Latter Day Saint)">
       restoration
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/One_true_church#Latter_Day_Saints" title="One true church">
       original church
      </a>
      founded by
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity" title="Jesus in Christianity">
       Jesus Christ
      </a>
      . The church is headquartered in
      <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">
       Salt Lake City
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">
       Utah
      </a>
      , and has established congregations (called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">
        wards
       </a>
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       branches
      </i>
      ) and built
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_(LDS_Church)" title="Temple (LDS Church)">
       temples
      </a>
      worldwide. According to the church, it has over 85,000
      <a href="/wiki/Missionary_(LDS_Church)" title="Missionary (LDS Church)">
       missionaries
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics_2014_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Statistics_2014-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_membership_statistics" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints membership statistics">
       membership
      </a>
      of over 15 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics_2014_2-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Statistics_2014-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is ranked by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Churches" title="National Council of Churches">
       National Council of Churches
      </a>
      as the fourth largest
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">
       Christian denomination
      </a>
      in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is by far the largest denomination in the
      <a href="/wiki/Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="Latter Day Saint movement">
       Latter Day Saint movement
      </a>
      founded by
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">
       Joseph Smith
      </a>
      during the period of religious revival known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Great_Awakening" title="Second Great Awakening">
       Second Great Awakening
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Adherents, sometimes referred to as
      <i>
       Latter-day Saints
      </i>
      or, less formally,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">
        Mormons
       </a>
      </i>
      , view faith in Jesus Christ and his
      <a href="/wiki/Atonement_in_Christianity" title="Atonement in Christianity">
       atonement
      </a>
      as the central tenet of their religion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      LDS theology includes the Christian doctrine of
      <a href="/wiki/Salvation_(Christianity)" title="Salvation (Christianity)">
       salvation
      </a>
      only through Jesus Christ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      though LDS doctrines regarding the
      <a href="/wiki/God_in_Mormonism" title="God in Mormonism">
       nature of God
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Mormonism)" title="Exaltation (Mormonism)">
       potential of mankind
      </a>
      differ significantly from mainstream Christianity. The church has an
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_canon" title="Biblical canon">
       open canon
      </a>
      which includes four
      <a href="/wiki/Religious_text" title="Religious text">
       scriptural texts
      </a>
      :
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the Bible (both
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">
       Old
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
       New Testaments
      </a>
      ), the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Mormon" title="Book of Mormon">
       Book of Mormon
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Doctrine_and_Covenants" title="Doctrine and Covenants">
       Doctrine and Covenants
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Pearl_of_Great_Price_(Mormonism)" title="Pearl of Great Price (Mormonism)">
       Pearl of Great Price
      </a>
      . Other than the Bible, the majority of the LDS canon constitutes revelation spoken by Joseph Smith and recorded by his scribes which includes commentary and
      <a href="/wiki/Exegesis" title="Exegesis">
       exegesis
      </a>
      about the Bible, texts described as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apocryphal" title="Apocryphal">
       lost parts of the Bible
      </a>
      , and other works believed to be written by ancient
      <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">
       prophets
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Under the doctrine of
      <a href="/wiki/Continuous_revelation" title="Continuous revelation">
       continuing
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Revelation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Revelation (Latter Day Saints)">
       revelation
      </a>
      , Latter-day Saints believe that Jesus Christ, under the direction of
      <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">
       God the Father
      </a>
      , leads the church by revealing his will to its
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Church_(LDS_Church)" title="President of the Church (LDS Church)">
       president
      </a>
      , whom adherents regard as a modern-day "
      <a href="/wiki/Prophet,_seer,_and_revelator" title="Prophet, seer, and revelator">
       prophet, seer, and revelator
      </a>
      ". The current president is
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">
       Thomas S. Monson
      </a>
      . Individual members believe that they can also receive personal
      <a href="/wiki/Revelation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Revelation (Latter Day Saints)">
       revelation
      </a>
      from God in conducting their lives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The president heads a hierarchical structure with various levels reaching down to local congregations.
      <a href="/wiki/Bishop_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Bishop (Latter Day Saints)">
       Bishops
      </a>
      , drawn from the
      <a href="/wiki/Laity" title="Laity">
       laity
      </a>
      , lead local congregations. Male members, after reaching age 12, may be ordained to the
      <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_(LDS_Church)" title="Priesthood (LDS Church)">
       priesthood
      </a>
      , provided they are living the standards of the church. Women do not hold positions within the priesthood, but do occupy leadership roles in church
      <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_organization_(LDS_Church)" title="Auxiliary organization (LDS Church)">
       auxiliary organizations
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ballard2007_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ballard2007-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Both men and women may serve as missionaries, and the church maintains a large missionary program which
      <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">
       proselytizes
      </a>
      and conducts
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Humanitarian_Services" title="LDS Humanitarian Services">
       humanitarian services
      </a>
      worldwide. Faithful members adhere to laws regarding
      <a href="/wiki/Law_of_chastity" title="Law of chastity">
       sexual purity
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Word_of_Wisdom" title="Word of Wisdom">
       health
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fasting#Mormonism" title="Fasting">
       fasting
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Sabbath_in_Christianity#The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Sabbath in Christianity">
       Sabbath observance
      </a>
      , and contribute ten percent of their income to the church as a
      <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">
       tithe
      </a>
      . In addition, the church teaches sacred
      <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Ordinance (Latter Day Saints)">
       ordinances
      </a>
      through which adherents make
      <a href="/wiki/Covenant_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Covenant (Latter Day Saints)">
       covenants
      </a>
      with God, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptism_(Mormonism)" title="Baptism (Mormonism)">
       baptism
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Confirmation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Confirmation (Latter Day Saints)">
       confirmation
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Sacrament_(LDS_Church)" title="Sacrament (LDS Church)">
       sacrament
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">
       holy communion
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Endowment_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Endowment (Latter Day Saints)">
       endowment
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Celestial_marriage" title="Celestial marriage">
       celestial marriage
      </a>
      (marriage blessings which extend beyond mortality)all of which are of great significance to church members.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="History of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       History of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The history of the LDS Church is typically divided into three broad time periods: (1) the early history during the lifetime of
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">
       Joseph Smith
      </a>
      , which is in common with all Latter Day Saint movement churches; (2) a pioneer era under the leadership of
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">
       Brigham Young
      </a>
      and his 19th-century successors; and (3) a modern era beginning around the turn of the 20th century as
      <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">
       Utah
      </a>
      achieved statehood.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">
       Beginnings
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="381" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg/170px-Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg/255px-Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg/340px-Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Smith_first_vision_stained_glass.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Church members believe that
        <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">
         Joseph Smith
        </a>
        was called to be a modern-day prophet through, among other events, a
        <a href="/wiki/First_Vision" title="First Vision">
         visitation
        </a>
        from
        <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">
         God the Father
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">
         Jesus Christ
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="History of the Latter Day Saint movement">
       History of the Latter Day Saint movement
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Church of Christ (Latter Day Saints)">
       Church of Christ (Latter Day Saints)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church was formally organized by
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">
       Joseph Smith
      </a>
      on April 6, 1830, in
      <a href="/wiki/Burned-over_district" title="Burned-over district">
       western New York
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Initial converts were drawn to the church in part because of the newly published
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Mormon" title="Book of Mormon">
       Book of Mormon
      </a>
      , a self-described chronicle of
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
       indigenous American
      </a>
      prophets that Smith said he had translated from
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_plates" title="Golden plates">
       golden plates
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Smith intended to establish the
      <a href="/wiki/New_Jerusalem" title="New Jerusalem">
       New Jerusalem
      </a>
      in North America, called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Zion_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Zion (Latter Day Saints)">
        Zion
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1831, the church moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Kirtland,_Ohio" title="Kirtland, Ohio">
       Kirtland, Ohio
      </a>
      (the eastern boundary of Zion),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and began establishing an outpost in
      <a href="/wiki/Jackson_County,_Missouri" title="Jackson County, Missouri">
       Jackson County, Missouri
      </a>
      (Zion's "center place"),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      where he planned to eventually move the church headquarters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in 1833, Missouri settlers brutally expelled the Latter Day Saints from Jackson County,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the church was unable via a
      <a href="/wiki/Zion%27s_Camp" title="Zion's Camp">
       paramilitary expedition
      </a>
      to recover the land.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, the church flourished in Kirtland
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as Smith published new revelations and the church built the
      <a href="/wiki/Kirtland_Temple" title="Kirtland Temple">
       Kirtland Temple
      </a>
      , culminating in a dedication of the building similar to the day of
      <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">
       Pentecost
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Kirtland era ended in 1838, after a
      <a href="/wiki/Kirtland_Safety_Society" title="Kirtland Safety Society">
       financial scandal
      </a>
      rocked the church and caused widespread defections.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith regrouped with the remaining church in
      <a href="/wiki/Far_West,_Missouri" title="Far West, Missouri">
       Far West, Missouri
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but tensions soon escalated into
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_War_(1838)" title="Mormon War (1838)">
       violent conflicts
      </a>
      with the old Missouri settlers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Believing the Saints to be in insurrection, the
      <a href="/wiki/Lilburn_Boggs" title="Lilburn Boggs">
       Missouri governor
      </a>
      ordered that the Saints be
      <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Executive_Order_44" title="Missouri Executive Order 44">
       "exterminated or driven from the State
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1839, the Saints converted a swampland on the banks of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
       Mississippi River
      </a>
      into
      <a href="/wiki/Nauvoo,_Illinois" title="Nauvoo, Illinois">
       Nauvoo, Illinois
      </a>
      , which became the church's new headquarters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nauvoo grew rapidly as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_missionary" title="Mormon missionary">
       missionaries
      </a>
      sent to Europe and elsewhere gained new converts who then flooded into Nauvoo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Meanwhile, Smith introduced
      <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">
       polygamy
      </a>
      to his closest associates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also established
      <a href="/wiki/Sealing_(Mormonism)" title="Sealing (Mormonism)">
       ceremonies
      </a>
      , which he stated the Lord had revealed to him, to allow righteous people to
      <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Mormonism)" title="Exaltation (Mormonism)">
       become gods
      </a>
      (joint heirs with Christ, see
      <a href="/wiki/Divinization_(Christian)" title="Divinization (Christian)">
       theosis
      </a>
      )
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in the afterlife,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Fifty" title="Council of Fifty">
       secular institution
      </a>
      to govern the
      <a href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">
       Millennial
      </a>
      kingdom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also introduced the church to a full accounting of his
      <a href="/wiki/First_Vision" title="First Vision">
       First Vision
      </a>
      , in which two heavenly "personages" (
      <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">
       God the Father
      </a>
      and his Son,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">
       Jesus Christ
      </a>
      ) appeared to him at age 14. This vision would come to be regarded by the LDS Church as the most important event in human history since the
      <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">
       resurrection of Jesus
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 27, 1844, Smith and his brother
      <a href="/wiki/Hyrum_Smith" title="Hyrum Smith">
       Hyrum
      </a>
      were
      <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Joseph_Smith" title="Death of Joseph Smith">
       murdered by a mob
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Carthage,_Illinois" title="Carthage, Illinois">
       Carthage, Illinois
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while being held on charges of treason.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Because Hyrum was Joseph's designated successor,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      their deaths caused a
      <a href="/wiki/Succession_crisis_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Succession crisis (Latter Day Saints)">
       succession crisis
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">
       Brigham Young
      </a>
      assumed leadership over the majority of Saints.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Young had been a close associate of Smith's and was senior
      <a href="/wiki/Apostle_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Apostle (Latter Day Saints)">
       apostle
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve" title="Quorum of the Twelve">
       Quorum of the Twelve
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other splinter groups followed other leaders in their own interpretation of the Latter Day Saint movement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pioneer_era">
       Pioneer era
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pioneer era">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BrighamYoung1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="496" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BrighamYoung1.jpg/220px-BrighamYoung1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BrighamYoung1.jpg/330px-BrighamYoung1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BrighamYoung1.jpg/440px-BrighamYoung1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BrighamYoung1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">
         Brigham Young
        </a>
        led the LDS Church from 1844 until his death in 1877.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      For two years after Smith's death, conflicts escalated between Mormons and other Illinois residents. To prevent war,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smith had predicted that the church would go to the West and be established in the tops of the Rocky Mountains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">
       Brigham Young
      </a>
      took Smith's advice and led his followers, known in modern times as the
      <a href="/wiki/Mormon_pioneers" title="Mormon pioneers">
       Mormon pioneers
      </a>
      , to
      <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">
       Nebraska
      </a>
      and then in 1847 to what became the
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Territory" title="Utah Territory">
       Utah Territory
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emigration-religious-freedom_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-emigration-religious-freedom-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As groups (over 60,000) arrived over a period of years, LDS settlers branched out and colonized a large region now known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Mormon_Corridor" title="Mormon Corridor">
       Mormon Corridor
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Young incorporated the LDS Church as a legal entity, and initially governed both the church and the state as a
      <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">
       theocratic
      </a>
      leader. He also publicized the practice of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plural_marriage" title="Plural marriage">
       plural marriage
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">
       polygamy
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      By 1857, tensions had again escalated between Mormons and other Americans, largely as a result of accusations involving polygamy and the theocratic rule of the Utah Territory by Young.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_War" title="Utah War">
       Utah Mormon War
      </a>
      ensued from 1857 to 1858, which resulted in the relatively peaceful
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      invasion of Utah by the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">
       United States Army
      </a>
      , after which Young agreed to step down from power and be replaced by a non-Mormon territorial governor,
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Cumming_(governor)" title="Alfred Cumming (governor)">
       Alfred Cumming
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, the LDS Church still wielded significant political power in the Utah Territory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At Young's death in 1877, he was followed by other church presidents, who resisted efforts by the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       United States Congress
      </a>
      to outlaw Mormon polygamous marriages. In 1878, the United States Supreme Court, in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Reynolds_v._United_States" title="Reynolds v. United States">
        Reynolds v. United States
       </a>
      </i>
      , decreed that "religious duty" to engage in plural marriage was not a valid defense to prosecutions for violating state laws against polygamy. Conflict between Mormons and the
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">
       U.S. government
      </a>
      escalated to the point that in 1890, Congress disincorporated the LDS Church and seized most of its assets. Soon thereafter, church president
      <a href="/wiki/Wilford_Woodruff" title="Wilford Woodruff">
       Wilford Woodruff
      </a>
      issued a
      <a href="/wiki/1890_Manifesto" title="1890 Manifesto">
       Manifesto
      </a>
      that officially suspended the practice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although this Manifesto did not dissolve existing plural marriages, so that families would not be split apart or damaged, no new polygamous marriages would be performed. Relations with the United States markedly improved after 1890, such that Utah was admitted as a U.S. state in 1896. Relations further improved after 1904, when church president
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_F._Smith" title="Joseph F. Smith">
       Joseph F. Smith
      </a>
      again
      <a href="/wiki/Reed_Smoot_hearings" title="Reed Smoot hearings">
       disavowed polygamy
      </a>
      before the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       United States Congress
      </a>
      and issued a "
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Manifesto" title="Second Manifesto">
       Second Manifesto
      </a>
      ", calling for all plural marriages in the church to cease, as they were already against church doctrine since Woodruff issued the Manifesto. Eventually, the church adopted a policy of
      <a href="/wiki/Excommunication" title="Excommunication">
       excommunicating
      </a>
      its members found practicing polygamy and today actively distances itself from "
      <a href="/wiki/Mormon_fundamentalism" title="Mormon fundamentalism">
       fundamentalist
      </a>
      " groups still practicing polygamy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times">
       Modern times
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern times">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salt_Lake_Temple,_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1367" data-file-width="1240" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg/220px-Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg/330px-Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg/440px-Salt_Lake_Temple%2C_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salt_Lake_Temple,_Utah_-_Sept_2004-2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Temple" title="Salt Lake Temple">
         Salt Lake Temple
        </a>
        , which took 40 years to build, is one of the most iconic images of the church.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the 20th century, the church grew substantially and became an international organization, due in part to the spread of missionaries around the globe. In 2000, the church reported 60,784 missionaries
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stats2000_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stats2000-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and global church membership stood at just over 11 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stats2000_54-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stats2000-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Worldwide membership surpassed 13 million in 2007
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and reached 14 million in July 2010,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-De_Groote_2011-01-23_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-De_Groote_2011-01-23-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with about six million of those within the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, it is estimated based on
      <a href="/wiki/Demography" title="Demography">
       demographic studies
      </a>
      from the early 1990s that only one-third of the total worldwide membership (about 4 million people as of 2005) are considered "active churchgoers."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stack_2005_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stack_2005-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church cautions against overemphasis of growth statistics for comparison with other churches because relevant factorsincluding activity rates and death rates, methodology used in registering or counting members, what factors constitute membership, and geographical variationsare rarely accounted for in the comparisons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The church has become a strong and public champion of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_family" title="Nuclear family">
       nuclear family
      </a>
      and at times played a prominent role in political matters, including opposition to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LGM-118A_Peacekeeper" title="LGM-118A Peacekeeper">
       MX Peacekeeper missile
      </a>
      bases in Utah and
      <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">
       Nevada
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Equal_Rights_Amendment" title="Equal Rights Amendment">
       Equal Rights Amendment
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      legalized gambling,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">
       same-sex marriage
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">
       physician-assisted death
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Apart from issues that it considers to be ones of morality, however, the church maintains a position of political neutrality, but encourages its members to be politically active, to participate in elections, and to be knowledgeable about current political and social issues within their communities, states, and countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of official changes have taken place to the organization during the modern era. One significant change was the ordination of men of black African descent to the priesthood in 1978, which reversed a policy originally instituted by Brigham Young in 1852.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bush_1984_p70_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bush_1984_p70-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are also periodic changes in the structure and organization of the church, mainly to accommodate the organization's growth and increasing international presence. For example, since the early 1900s, the church has instituted a
      <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_Correlation_Program" title="Priesthood Correlation Program">
       Priesthood Correlation Program
      </a>
      to centralize church operations and bring them under a hierarchy of priesthood leaders. During the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , the church also began operating a church welfare system, and it has conducted numerous humanitarian efforts in cooperation with other religious organizations including
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Relief_Services" title="Catholic Relief Services">
       Catholic Relief Services
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Relief" title="Islamic Relief">
       Islamic Relief
      </a>
      , as well as secular organizations such as the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">
       American Red Cross
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Teachings_and_practices">
       Teachings and practices
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Teachings and practices">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Authorized_texts">
       Authorized texts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Authorized texts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2264" data-file-width="1260" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg/130px-Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg/195px-Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg/260px-Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg 2x" width="130"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Latter-day_Saint_Scripture_Quadruple_Combination.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The written canon of the LDS Church is referred to as its
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Standard_works" title="Standard works">
          standard works
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The theology of the LDS Church consists of a combination of biblical doctrines with modern revelations and other commentary by LDS leaders, particularly Joseph Smith. The most authoritative sources of theology are the faith's canon of four religious texts, called the "
      <a href="/wiki/Standard_works" title="Standard works">
       standard works
      </a>
      ". Included in the standard works are the Bible, the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Mormon" title="Book of Mormon">
       Book of Mormon
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Doctrine_and_Covenants" title="Doctrine and Covenants">
       Doctrine and Covenants
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Pearl_of_Great_Price_(Mormonism)" title="Pearl of Great Price (Mormonism)">
       Pearl of Great Price
      </a>
      . The Book of Mormon is said by the church to be "Another Testament of Jesus Christ" that Smith translated from buried
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_plates" title="Golden plates">
       golden plates
      </a>
      . The LDS Church believes that the
      <a href="/wiki/Angel_Moroni" title="Angel Moroni">
       Angel Moroni
      </a>
      told Smith about these golden plates and guided him to find them buried in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hill_Cumorah" title="Hill Cumorah">
       Hill Cumorah
      </a>
      . The church believes that this Angel Moroni is at least partial fulfilment of Revelation 14:6 in the Bible. The church characterizes the Book of Mormon as "the most correct of any book on earth and the keystone of [the] religion".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Bible, also part of the church's canon, is believed to be "the word of God as far as it is translated correctly."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most often, the church uses the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authorized_King_James_Version" title="Authorized King James Version">
       Authorized King James Version
      </a>
      . Sometimes, however, parts of the
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith_Translation_of_the_Bible" title="Joseph Smith Translation of the Bible">
       Joseph Smith Translation of the Bible
      </a>
      (corrections and restorations of assertedly damaged or lost passages) are considered authoritative. Some excerpts of Smith's translation have been included in the Pearl of Great Price, which also includes further translations by Smith and church historical items. Other historical items and revelations are found in the Doctrine and Covenants.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another source of authoritative doctrine is the pronouncements of the current Apostles and members of the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Presidency_(LDS_Church)" title="First Presidency (LDS Church)">
       First Presidency
      </a>
      . The church teaches that the First Presidency (the church's president and his counselors) and the Quorum of Twelve Apostles are prophets
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oct12_conference_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-oct12_conference-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and that their teachings are generally given under inspiration from God through the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">
       Holy Spirit
      </a>
      . Members of the church
      <a href="/wiki/Common_consent_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Common consent (Latter Day Saints)">
       acknowledge (sustain)
      </a>
      them regularly as
      <a href="/wiki/Prophet,_seer,_and_revelator" title="Prophet, seer, and revelator">
       prophets, seers, and revelators
      </a>
      this is done publicly twice a year at the church's worldwide
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_conference_(LDS_Church)" title="General conference (LDS Church)">
       general conference
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oct12_conference_69-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-oct12_conference-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctive_doctrines_and_practices">
       Distinctive doctrines and practices
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Distinctive doctrines and practices">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Beliefs_and_practices_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Beliefs and practices of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       Beliefs and practices of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phil_and_Marlene.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="285" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phil_and_Marlene.jpg/170px-Phil_and_Marlene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phil_and_Marlene.jpg/255px-Phil_and_Marlene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5c/Phil_and_Marlene.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phil_and_Marlene.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A couple after their
        <a href="/wiki/Celestial_marriage" title="Celestial marriage">
         marriage
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Manti_Utah_Temple" title="Manti Utah Temple">
         Manti Utah Temple
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Several doctrines and practices of the LDS Church are peculiar within Christianity. For example, the
      <a href="/wiki/Mormon_cosmology" title="Mormon cosmology">
       Mormon cosmology
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Plan_of_salvation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Plan of salvation (Latter Day Saints)">
       plan of salvation
      </a>
      include the doctrines of a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-mortal_life" title="Pre-mortal life">
       pre-mortal life
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degrees_of_Glory" title="Degrees of Glory">
       three degrees of heaven
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Exaltation (Latter Day Saints)">
       exaltation
      </a>
      . According to these doctrines every human spirit is a literal child of
      <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">
       Heavenly Father
      </a>
      , and each has the potential to continue to learn, grow, and progress in the eternities, eventually achieving eternal life (which Latter-day Saints view distinct from
      <a href="/wiki/Immortality" title="Immortality">
       immortality
      </a>
      ), which is to become one with God in the same way that
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">
       Jesus Christ
      </a>
      is one with the Father, thus allowing the children of God to become divine beings or "gods" themselves,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the LDS view of
      <a href="/wiki/Divinization_(Christian)" title="Divinization (Christian)">
       theosis
      </a>
      , also referred to as becoming a "joint-heir with Christ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoM_Godhood_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EoM_Godhood-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The process by which this is accomplished is called
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Exaltation (Latter Day Saints)">
        exaltation
       </a>
      </i>
      , a doctrine which includes the reunification of the mortal family after the
      <a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">
       resurrection
      </a>
      and the ability to have spirit children in the afterlife and inherit a portion of God's kingdom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoM_Godhood_71-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-EoM_Godhood-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To obtain this state of godhood, the church teaches that one must have faith in Jesus Christ,
      <a href="/wiki/Repentance" title="Repentance">
       repent
      </a>
      of his or her sins, strive to keep the commandments faithfully, and participate in a sequence of ceremonial
      <a href="/wiki/Covenant_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Covenant (Latter Day Saints)">
       covenants
      </a>
      called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Ordinance (Latter Day Saints)">
        ordinances
       </a>
      </i>
      , which include
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptism_(LDS_Church)" title="Baptism (LDS Church)">
       baptism
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Confirmation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Confirmation (Latter Day Saints)">
       receiving the gift of the Holy Ghost
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Endowment_(Mormonism)" title="Endowment (Mormonism)">
       endowment
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Celestial_marriage" title="Celestial marriage">
       celestial marriage
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      This latter ordinance, known as a
      <a href="/wiki/Sealing_(Mormonism)" title="Sealing (Mormonism)">
       sealing
      </a>
      ceremony, reflects a singular LDS view with respect to families. According to LDS Church theology, men and women may be "sealed" to one another so that their marital bond continues into the eternities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Children may also be sealed to their biological or adoptive parents to form permanent familial bonds, thus allowing all immediate and extended family relations to endure past death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The most significant LDS ordinances may be performed via proxy in behalf of those who have died, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Baptism_for_the_dead" title="Baptism for the dead">
       baptism for the dead
      </a>
      . The church teaches that all will have the opportunity to hear and accept or reject the gospel of Jesus Christ and the blessings that come to those who faithfully adhere to it, in this life or the next. Ordinances such as baptisms for the dead, sealings, and
      <a href="/wiki/Endowment_(Mormonism)" title="Endowment (Mormonism)">
       endowments
      </a>
      are performed in
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_(LDS_Church)" title="Temple (LDS Church)">
       temples
      </a>
      that are built and dedicated specifically for these purposes.
     </p>
     <p>
      The LDS faithful observe a health code called the "
      <a href="/wiki/Word_of_Wisdom" title="Word of Wisdom">
       Word of Wisdom
      </a>
      ," in which they abstain from the consumption of alcohol, coffee, tea, and tobacco.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wordofwisdom_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wordofwisdom-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Word of Wisdom also encourages the use of wholesome herbs and fruits within season, moderate consumption of meat, and consumption of grains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wordofwisdom_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-wordofwisdom-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Latter-day Saints follow a moral code, called the "
      <a href="/wiki/Law_of_chastity" title="Law of chastity">
       law of chastity
      </a>
      ," which prohibits
      <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">
       adultery
      </a>
      , all homosexual behavior, and any sexual relations outside of marriage.
     </p>
     <p>
      LDS faithful donate a ten percent
      <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">
       tithe
      </a>
      on their annual income, which is used to carry out the operations of the church, including construction of temples, meetinghouses and other buildings, as well as other church uses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tithe_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tithe-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Faithful members also set aside the
      <a href="/wiki/Fast_Sunday" title="Fast Sunday">
       first Sunday of each month
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">
       abstain from food and drink
      </a>
      for at least two consecutive meals, and prayerfully dedicate the fast to a purpose of the individuals' choosing. They donate at least the cost of the two skipped meals as a
      <a href="/wiki/Fast_offering" title="Fast offering">
       fast offering
      </a>
      , which the church uses to assist the poor and needy and expand its worldwide
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Humanitarian_Services" title="LDS Humanitarian Services">
       humanitarian efforts
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fastoffering_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fastoffering-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Members are further instructed to set aside one night a week, typically Monday, for a "
      <a href="/wiki/Family_Home_Evening" title="Family Home Evening">
       Family Home Evening
      </a>
      ," where they gather together as a family to study gospel principles and participate in wholesome activities.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Missionary_service">
       Missionary service
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Missionary service">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="1712" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG/170px-MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG/255px-MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG/340px-MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MISSIONNAIRES_MORMONS.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Missionary_(LDS_Church)" title="Missionary (LDS Church)">
         Missionaries
        </a>
        typically commit to 1824 months of full-time service.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Missionary_(LDS_Church)" title="Missionary (LDS Church)">
       Missionary (LDS Church)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      All LDS young men are expected to serve a two-year, full-time proselytizing mission.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Missionaries do not choose where they serve or the language in which they will proselytize, and are expected to fund their missions themselves or with the aid of their families. Prospective male missionaries must be at least 18 years old and no older than 25, not yet married, have completed secondary school, and meet certain criteria for physical fitness and spiritual worthiness. Missionary service is not compulsory, nor is it required for young men to retain their church membership. Unmarried women 19 years and older may also serve as missionaries, generally for a term of 18 months. However, the LDS Church emphasizes that women are not under the same expectation to serve as male members are, and may serve solely as a personal decision. There is no maximum age for missionary service for women.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prior to October 2012, the minimum age for full-time missionary service was generally 19 for men and 21 for women.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Retired couples are encouraged to serve missions, and may serve for either 6-, 12-, 18-, or 23-month terms.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Unlike younger missionaries, these senior missionaries may serve in non-proselytizing capacities such as
      <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">
       humanitarian aid
      </a>
      workers or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_history" title="Family history">
       family history
      </a>
      specialists.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Comparisons_with_mainstream_Christianity">
       Comparisons with mainstream Christianity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Comparisons with mainstream Christianity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Mormonism_and_Christianity" title="Mormonism and Christianity">
       Mormonism and Christianity
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church shares various teachings with other branches of Christianity. These include a belief in the Bible (subject to an acknowledgement that it is imperfect),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the divinity of Jesus, and his
      <a href="/wiki/Atonement_in_Christianity" title="Atonement in Christianity">
       atonement
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus_Christ" title="Resurrection of Jesus Christ">
       resurrection
      </a>
      . LDS theology also includes belief in the doctrine of salvation through Jesus alone,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restorationism_(Christian_primitivism)" title="Restorationism (Christian primitivism)">
       restorationism
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">
       millennialism
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Continuationism" title="Continuationism">
       continuationism
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Penal_substitution" title="Penal substitution">
       penal substitution
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_succession" title="Apostolic succession">
       apostolic succession
      </a>
      . The practices of
      <a href="/wiki/Baptism#Submersion" title="Baptism">
       baptism by immersion
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">
       eucharist
      </a>
      (referred to as
      <i>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Sacrament_(LDS_Church)" title="Sacrament (LDS Church)">
        sacrament
       </a>
      </i>
      ) are also held in common. However, the
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
       Catholic Church
      </a>
      considers doctrinal differences between the two groups to be so great that it will not accept a prior LDS baptism as evidence of Christian initiation, as it will baptism by other Christian groups, such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">
       Eastern Orthodox
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
       Protestant
      </a>
      churches.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The LDS Church does not accept baptisms performed in other churches.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nevertheless, the LDS Church differs from the many other churches within contemporary Christianity, and many people do not accept the church as part of Christianity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The faith itself views other modern Christian faiths as having departed from true Christianity
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      via a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_apostasy" title="Great apostasy">
       general apostasy
      </a>
      and maintains that it is a restoration of 1st-century Christianity and the only true and authorized Christian church.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Differences between the LDS Church and most of traditional Christianity include disagreement with aspects of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">
       Nicene Creed
      </a>
      , belief in a unique theory of
      <a href="/wiki/Plan_of_salvation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Plan of salvation (Latter Day Saints)">
       human salvation
      </a>
      that includes three heavens (referred to as "
      <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_glory" title="Degrees of glory">
       degrees of glory
      </a>
      ", its interpretation of I Cor. 15:35
      <i>
       et.seq.
      </i>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a doctrine of "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Exaltation (Latter Day Saints)">
       exaltation
      </a>
      " which includes the ability of humans to become gods and goddesses in the
      <a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">
       afterlife
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EoM_Godhood_71-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-EoM_Godhood-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a dietary code called the
      <a href="/wiki/Word_of_Wisdom" title="Word of Wisdom">
       Word of Wisdom
      </a>
      , and unique ceremonies performed privately in
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_(LDS_Church)" title="Temple (LDS Church)">
       LDS temples
      </a>
      , such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Endowment_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Endowment (Latter Day Saints)">
       endowment
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sealing_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Sealing (Latter Day Saints)">
       sealing
      </a>
      ceremonies.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1067" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg/220px-Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg/330px-Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg/440px-Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christus_statue_temple_square_salt_lake_city.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Latter-day Saints believe in the
        <a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">
         resurrection
        </a>
        of Jesus, as depicted in this replica of
        <a href="/wiki/Bertel_Thorvaldsen" title="Bertel Thorvaldsen">
         Bertel Thorvaldsen
        </a>
        's
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Christus_(statue)" title="Christus (statue)">
          Christus
         </a>
        </i>
        statue located in the North Visitors' Center on
        <a href="/wiki/Temple_Square" title="Temple Square">
         Temple Square
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">
         Salt Lake City
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Officially, major Christian denominations view the LDS Church as standing apart from
      <a href="/wiki/Creed" title="Creed">
       creedal
      </a>
      Christianity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Leaders of the LDS Church assert that the LDS Church is the only true church and that other churches do not have the authority to act in Jesus' name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From the perspective of Christians who agree with creeds, the most significant area of departure is the rejection by the LDS Church of certain parts of ecumenical creeds such as the Nicene Creed, which defines the predominant view of the Christian God as a
      <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">
       Trinity
      </a>
      of three separate persons in "
      <a href="/wiki/Homoousian" title="Homoousian">
       one essence
      </a>
      ". LDS Church theology includes the belief in a "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Godhead_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Godhead (Latter Day Saints)">
       Godhead
      </a>
      " composed of God the Father, his Son Jesus Christ, and the Holy Ghost as three separate Persons who share a unity of purpose or will; however, they are viewed as three distinct Beings making one Godhead. Other significant differences relate to the church's acceptance of additional scripture, doctrine, and practices beyond what is found in the Catholic, Protestant, or
      <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      versions of the Bible.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_with_other_Latter_Day_Saint_movement_faiths">
       Comparison with other Latter Day Saint movement faiths
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Comparison with other Latter Day Saint movement faiths">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_sects_in_the_Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="List of sects in the Latter Day Saint movement">
       List of sects in the Latter Day Saint movement
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church shares a common heritage with a number of smaller faith groups that are collectively called the
      <a href="/wiki/Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="Latter Day Saint movement">
       Latter Day Saint movement
      </a>
      . The largest of these smaller groups is the
      <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Christ" title="Community of Christ">
       Community of Christ
      </a>
