      (previously known as the Reorganized Church of Jesus Christ of Latter Day Saints), based in
      <a href="/wiki/Independence,_Missouri" title="Independence, Missouri">
       Independence, Missouri
      </a>
      , followed by the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_(Bickertonite)" title="The Church of Jesus Christ (Bickertonite)">
       The Church of Jesus Christ
      </a>
      , based in
      <a href="/wiki/Monongahela,_Pennsylvania" title="Monongahela, Pennsylvania">
       Monongahela, Pennsylvania
      </a>
      . Like the LDS Church, these faiths believe in Joseph Smith as a prophet and founder of their religion. They also accept the Book of Mormon, and most, but not all, accept at least some version of the
      <a href="/wiki/Doctrine_and_Covenants" title="Doctrine and Covenants">
       Doctrine and Covenants
      </a>
      . However, they tend to disagree to varying degrees with the LDS Church concerning doctrine and church leadership.
     </p>
     <p>
      The main branches of the Latter Day Saint movement resulted from the crisis of succession upon the death of Joseph Smith. Other branches may be considered later off-shoots of the LDS Church branch, mainly due to disagreements about plural marriage.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_structure">
       Organization and structure
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Organization and structure">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_legal_entities">
       Name and legal entities
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Name and legal entities">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Name_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Name of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       Name of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City,_Utah_(cropped).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1194" data-file-width="2269" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg/600px-LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City%2C_Utah_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LDS_stake_center_in_West_Valley_City,_Utah_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A typical
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meetinghouse" title="Meetinghouse">
         meetinghouse
        </a>
        of the church, where Sunday worship and social gatherings during the week convene
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The church teaches that it is a continuation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Church of Christ (Latter Day Saints)">
       Church of Christ
      </a>
      established in 1830 by Joseph Smith. This original church underwent several name changes during the 1830s, being called the Church of Jesus Christ, the Church of God,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and then in 1834, the name was officially changed to the Church of the Latter Day Saints.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 1838, the name was officially changed to the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter Day Saints.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After Smith died, Brigham Young and the largest body of Smith's followers incorporated the LDS Church in 1851 by legislation of the
      <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">
       State of Deseret
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      under the name "The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints", which included a hyphenated "Latter-day" and a
      <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">
       British-style
      </a>
      lower-case "d."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1887, the LDS Church was legally dissolved in the United States by the
      <a href="/wiki/Edmunds%E2%80%93Tucker_Act" title="EdmundsTucker Act">
       EdmundsTucker Act
      </a>
      because of the church's practice of polygamy. (The EdmundsTucker Act was repealed in 1978.) In the United States, the church continues to operate as an unincorporated entity.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Accepted informal names for the church include the LDS Church, the Latter-day Saints, and the Mormons. The term
      <i>
       Mormon Church
      </i>
      is in common use,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but the church began discouraging its use in the late 20th century, though takes no issue with the term
      <i>
       Mormon
      </i>
      itself. The church requests that the official name be used when possible or, if necessary, shortened to "the Church" or "the Church of Jesus Christ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Tax-exempt corporations of the LDS Church include the
      <i>
       Corporation of the Presiding Bishop of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </i>
      , which was organized in 1916 under the laws of the state of Utah to acquire, hold, and dispose of
      <a href="/wiki/Real_property" title="Real property">
       real property
      </a>
      ; the
      <i>
       Corporation of the President of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </i>
      , which was established in 1923 in Utah to receive and manage money and church donations; and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_Reserve" title="Intellectual Reserve">
        Intellectual Reserve, Inc.
       </a>
      </i>
      , which was incorporated in 1997 to hold the church's
      <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">
       copyrights
      </a>
      , trademarks, and other intellectual property. Non-tax-exempt corporations of the church include
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonneville_International_Corporation" title="Bonneville International Corporation">
       Bonneville International
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Deseret_News" title="Deseret News">
       Deseret News
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution_and_membership">
       Geographic distribution and membership
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution and membership">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_membership_statistics" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints membership statistics">
       The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints membership statistics
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_membership_history" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints membership history">
       The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints membership history
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LDS_Church_presence_2008.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LDS_Church_presence_2008.png/300px-LDS_Church_presence_2008.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LDS_Church_presence_2008.png/450px-LDS_Church_presence_2008.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LDS_Church_presence_2008.png/600px-LDS_Church_presence_2008.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LDS_Church_presence_2008.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #336699; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Countries and territories with at least one LDS temple
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #99CCFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Countries and territories with no LDS temple, but with organized congregations and/or missionaries
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CCCCCC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Countries and territories with no official LDS presence
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Church congregations are organized geographically. Members are generally expected to attend the congregation with their assigned geographical area; however, some geographical areas also provide separate congregations for young single adults (between the ages of 18 and 30), single adults aged 31 to 45,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or for speakers of alternate languages. For Sunday services, the church is grouped into either larger (~150 to ~400 people) congregations known as
      <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">
       wards
      </a>
      , or smaller congregations known as branches. Although the building may sometimes be referred to as a chapel, the room used as a chapel for religious services is actually only one component of the standard
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meetinghouse" title="Meetinghouse">
       meetinghouse
      </a>
      , of which the church maintains a virtual tour of a typical example and also an online meetinghouse locator which can be used to find the locations and meeting times of its congregations all over the world. Regional church organizations encompassing multiple congregations include
      <a href="/wiki/Stake_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Stake (Latter Day Saints)">
       stakes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mission_(LDS_Church)" title="Mission (LDS Church)">
       missions
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/District_(LDS_Church)" title="District (LDS Church)">
       districts
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Area_(LDS_Church)" title="Area (LDS Church)">
       areas
      </a>
      , and regions.
     </p>
     <table align="right" border="1" cellpadding="2" class="wikitable">
      <tr>
       <th width="200">
        2012 Pew Forum on Religion &amp; Public Life Survey
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_103-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-pew-103">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          103
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </th>
       <th width="25">
        Mormons (U.S.)
       </th>
       <th width="25">
        U.S. Avg.
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        Married
       </td>
       <td>
        67%
       </td>
       <td>
        52%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        Divorced or separated
       </td>
       <td>
        9%
       </td>
       <td>
        13%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        3 or more children at home
       </td>
       <td>
        21%
       </td>
       <td>
        9%
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        Attendance at religious services (weekly or more)
       </td>
       <td>
        77%
       </td>
       <td>
        39%
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The church reports a worldwide membership of 15million
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with approximately 8.3 million residing outside the United States, as of December 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to these statistics it is the fourth largest religious body in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church membership report includes all baptized members and their children. Although the church does not release attendance figures to the public, researchers estimate that actual attendance at weekly LDS worship services globally is around 4million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stack_2005_58-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Stack_2005-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Members living in the U.S. and Canada constitute 46% percent of membership, Latin America 38 percent, and members in the rest of the world 16 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-currentmembership_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-currentmembership-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 2012
      <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">
       Pew Forum on Religion &amp; Public Life
      </a>
      survey, conducted by Princeton Survey Research Associates International, found that approximately 2 percent of the U.S. adult population self identified as Mormon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_103-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pew-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The church continues to seek recognition in regions where it has had little or no influence. On August 30, 2010, church leaders announced that they were making significant progress on "regularized operations for the Church in China."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-china_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-china-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For a list of notable Latter-day Saints, see
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Latter_Day_Saints" title="List of Latter Day Saints">
       List of Latter Day Saints
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Priesthood_hierarchy">
       Priesthood hierarchy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Priesthood hierarchy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_(LDS_Church)" title="Priesthood (LDS Church)">
       Priesthood (LDS Church)
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_S_Monson.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1920" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Thomas_S_Monson.jpg/220px-Thomas_S_Monson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Thomas_S_Monson.jpg/330px-Thomas_S_Monson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Thomas_S_Monson.jpg/440px-Thomas_S_Monson.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_S_Monson.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">
         Thomas S. Monson
        </a>
        , President of the LDS Church since 2008.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church is organized in a hierarchical priesthood structure administered by men. Latter-day Saints believe that
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">
       Jesus
      </a>
      leads the church through revelation and has chosen a single man, called "the Prophet" or President of the Church, as his spokesman on the earth. The current president is
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">
       Thomas S. Monson
      </a>
      . While there have been exceptions in the past, he and two counselors are normally ordained
      <a href="/wiki/Apostle_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Apostle (Latter Day Saints)">
       apostles
      </a>
      and form the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Presidency_(LDS_Church)" title="First Presidency (LDS Church)">
       First Presidency
      </a>
      , the presiding body of the church; twelve other apostles form the
      <a href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve_Apostles_(LDS_Church)" title="Quorum of the Twelve Apostles (LDS Church)">
       Quorum of the Twelve Apostles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haight.2C_David_B._1986_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Haight.2C_David_B._1986-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When a president dies, his successor is invariably the most senior member of the Quorum of the Twelve (the one who has been an apostle the longest), who then reconstitutes a new First Presidency.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haight.2C_David_B._1986_111-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Haight.2C_David_B._1986-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These men, and the other male members of the church-wide leadership (including the first two
      <a href="/wiki/Seventy_(LDS_Church)" title="Seventy (LDS Church)">
       Quorums of Seventy
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presiding_Bishopric" title="Presiding Bishopric">
       Presiding Bishopric
      </a>
      ) are called
      <a href="/wiki/General_authority" title="General authority">
       general authorities
      </a>
      . They exercise both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical" title="Ecclesiastical">
       ecclesiastical
      </a>
      and administrative leadership over the church and direct the efforts of regional leaders down to the local level. General authorities and
      <a href="/wiki/Mission_president" title="Mission president">
       mission presidents
      </a>
      work full-time and typically receive stipends from church funds or investments.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the local level, the church leadership are drawn from the laity and work on a part-time volunteer basis without stipend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Like all members, they are asked to donate a tithe of 10 percent of their income to the church. An exception to that rule is for LDS missionaries who work at the local level and are paid basic living expenses from a fund that receives contributions from their families or home congregations; however, prospective missionaries are encouraged to contribute the cost of their missions to this fund themselves when possible. Members volunteer general custodial work for local church facilities.
     </p>
     <div class="center">
      <div class="thumb tnone">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1837" data-file-width="6062" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg/700px-LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg/1050px-LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg/1400px-LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg 2x" width="700"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LDS_Conference_Center_interior_panoramic.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Interior of the
         <a href="/wiki/LDS_Conference_Center" title="LDS Conference Center">
          Conference Center
         </a>
         where the church holds its
         <a href="/wiki/General_Conference_(LDS_Church)" title="General Conference (LDS Church)">
          General Conferences
         </a>
         twice a year.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      All males who are living the standards of the church are generally considered for the
      <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Priesthood (Latter Day Saints)">
       priesthood
      </a>
      and are ordained to the priesthood as early as age 12. Ordination occurs by a ceremony where
      <a href="/wiki/Laying_on_of_hands" title="Laying on of hands">
       hands are laid
      </a>
      on the head of the one ordained. The priesthood is divided into an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aaronic_priesthood_(LDS_Church)" title="Aaronic priesthood (LDS Church)">
       Aaronic priesthood
      </a>
      for young men 12 and up and a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melchizedek_Priesthood_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Melchizedek Priesthood (Latter Day Saints)">
       Melchizedek priesthood
      </a>
      for men 18 and up.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Programs_and_auxiliary_organizations">
       Programs and auxiliary organizations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Programs and auxiliary organizations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_organization_(LDS_Church)" title="Auxiliary organization (LDS Church)">
       Auxiliary organization (LDS Church)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Under the leadership of the priesthood hierarchy are five auxiliary organizations that fill various roles in the church:
      <a href="/wiki/Relief_Society" title="Relief Society">
       Relief Society
      </a>
      (a women's organization),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Young_Men_organization" title="Young Men organization">
       Young Men
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Women_(organization)" title="Young Women (organization)">
       Young Women
      </a>
      organizations (for adolescents ages 12 to 18),
      <a href="/wiki/Primary_(LDS_Church)" title="Primary (LDS Church)">
       Primary
      </a>
      (an organization for children up to age 12), and
      <a href="/wiki/Sunday_School_(LDS_Church)" title="Sunday School (LDS Church)">
       Sunday School
      </a>
      (which provides a variety of Sunday classes for adolescents and adults). Women serve as presidents and counselors in the presidencies of the Relief Society, Young Women, and Primary, while men serve as presidents and counselors of the Young Men and Sunday School.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church also operates several programs and organizations in the fields of proselytizing, education, and church welfare such as
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Humanitarian_Services" title="LDS Humanitarian Services">
       LDS Humanitarian Services
      </a>
      . Many of these auxiliaries and programs are coordinated by the
      <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_Correlation_Program" title="Priesthood Correlation Program">
       Priesthood Correlation Program
      </a>
      , which is designed to provide a systematic approach to maintain worldwide consistency, orthodoxy, and control of the church's ordinances, doctrines, organizations, meetings, materials, and other programs and activities.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BYUclarillon.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/BYUclarillon.jpg/220px-BYUclarillon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/BYUclarillon.jpg/330px-BYUclarillon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/BYUclarillon.jpg/440px-BYUclarillon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BYUclarillon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University_Centennial_Carillon_Tower" title="Brigham Young University Centennial Carillon Tower">
         carillon tower
        </a>
        at
        <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">
         Brigham Young University
        </a>
        , one of several educational institutions sponsored by the church
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The church operates a
      <a href="/wiki/Church_Educational_System" title="Church Educational System">
       Church Educational System
      </a>
      which includes
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">
       Brigham Young University
      </a>
      (BYU) (and its associated
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University_Jerusalem_Center" title="Brigham Young University Jerusalem Center">
       Jerusalem Center
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University%E2%80%93Idaho" title="Brigham Young UniversityIdaho">
       BYUIdaho
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University%E2%80%93Hawaii" title="Brigham Young UniversityHawaii">
       BYUHawaii
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Business_College" title="LDS Business College">
       LDS Business College
      </a>
      . The church also operates
      <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Religion" title="Institute of Religion">
       Institutes of Religion
      </a>
      near the campuses of many colleges and universities. For high-school aged youth, the church operates a four-year
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LDS_Seminary" title="LDS Seminary">
       Seminary program
      </a>
      , which provides religious classes for students to supplement their secular education. The church also sponsors a low-interest educational loan program known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_Education_Fund" title="Perpetual Education Fund">
       Perpetual Education Fund
      </a>
      , which provides educational opportunities to students from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nations" title="Developing nations">
       developing nations
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MormonNewsroom.org_Education_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MormonNewsroom.org_Education-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg/220px-LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg/330px-LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg/440px-LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LDS_genealogy_library_slc_utah.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The church's
        <a href="/wiki/Family_History_Library" title="Family History Library">
         Family History Library
        </a>
        is the world's largest library dedicated to
        <a href="/wiki/Genealogy" title="Genealogy">
         genealogical research
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The church's welfare system, initiated during the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , provides aid to the poor. It is financed by
      <a href="/wiki/Fast_offering" title="Fast offering">
       fast offerings
      </a>
      : monthly donations beyond the normal 10 percent tithe, which represents the cost of forgoing two meals on monthly
      <a href="/wiki/Fast_Sunday" title="Fast Sunday">
       Fast Sundays
      </a>
      . Money from the program is used to operate
      <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_storehouse" title="Bishop's storehouse">
       Bishop's storehouses
      </a>
      , which package and store food at low cost. Distribution of funds and food is administered by local
      <a href="/wiki/Bishop_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Bishop (Latter Day Saints)">
       bishops
      </a>
      . The church also distributes money through its
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Philanthropies" title="LDS Philanthropies">
       LDS Philanthropies
      </a>
      division to disaster victims worldwide.
     </p>
     <p>
      Other church programs and departments include
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Family_Services" title="LDS Family Services">
       LDS Family Services
      </a>
      , which provides assistance with
      <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">
       adoption
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Relationship_counseling" title="Relationship counseling">
       marital and family counseling
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">
       psychotherapy
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Intervention_(counseling)" title="Intervention (counseling)">
       addiction counseling
      </a>
      ; the LDS Church History Department, which collects church history and records; and the Family History Department, which administers the church's large
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_history" title="Family history">
       family history
      </a>
      efforts, including the world's largest
      <a href="/wiki/Family_History_Library" title="Family History Library">
       family history library
      </a>
      and organization (
      <a href="/wiki/FamilySearch" title="FamilySearch">
       FamilySearch
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church is also a major sponsor of
      <a href="/wiki/Scouting" title="Scouting">
       Scouting
      </a>
      programs for boys, particularly in the United States, where it provides more
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boy_Scout" title="Boy Scout">
       members
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">
       Boy Scouts of America
      </a>
      than any other church.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">
       Finances
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Finances">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Finances_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Finances of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       Finances of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Although the church has not released church-wide financial statements since 1959, in 1997,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" title="Time Magazine">
        Time
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine called it one of the world's wealthiest churches per capita.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a June 2011 cover story,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">
        Newsweek
       </a>
      </i>
      stated that the LDS Church "resembles a sanctified multinational corporationthe General Electric of American religion, with global ambitions and an estimated net worth of $30 billion."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsMorm_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NewsMorm-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its for-profit, non-profit, and educational subsidiary entities are audited by an independent accounting firm: as of 2007
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , some done by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deloitte_%26_Touche" title="Deloitte &amp; Touche">
       Deloitte &amp; Touche
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, the church employs an independent
      <a href="/wiki/Audit" title="Audit">
       audit
      </a>
      department that provides its certification at each annual
      <a href="/wiki/General_Conference_(LDS_Church)" title="General Conference (LDS Church)">
       general conference
      </a>
      that church contributions are collected and spent in accordance with church policy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The church receives significant funds from
      <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">
       tithes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fast_offering" title="Fast offering">
       fast offerings
      </a>
      . According to the church, tithing and fast offering money collected are devoted to ecclesiastical purposes and not used in for-profit ventures.
     </p>
     <p>
      The church has also invested in for-profit business and real estate ventures such as
      <a href="/wiki/Bonneville_International" title="Bonneville International">
       Bonneville International
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deseret_Book_Company" title="Deseret Book Company">
       Deseret Book Company
      </a>
      , and cattle ranches in Utah, Florida, Nebraska, Canada and other locations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Culture of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       Culture of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Due to the differences in lifestyle promoted by church doctrine and history, a distinct culture has grown up around members of the LDS Church. It is primarily concentrated in the
      <a href="/wiki/Intermountain_West" title="Intermountain West">
       Intermountain West
      </a>
      , but as membership of the church spreads around the world, many of its more distinctive practices follow, such as adhering to the Word of Wisdom, a health law or code prohibiting the consumption of tobacco, alcohol, coffee, tea, and illegal drugs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wordofwisdom_77-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-wordofwisdom-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a result of the Word of Wisdom, the culture in areas of the world with a high concentration of LDS tends to be reflected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Meetings and outreach programs are held regularly and have become part of Latter-day Saint culture.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_arts">
       Media and arts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media and arts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The culture has created substantial business opportunities for independent LDS media. Such communities include
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_cinema" title="LDS cinema">
       cinema
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_fiction" title="LDS fiction">
       fiction
      </a>
      , websites, and graphical art like photography and paintings. The church owns a chain of bookstores called
      <a href="/wiki/Deseret_Book" title="Deseret Book">
       Deseret Book
      </a>
      , which provide a channel through which publications are sold. Titles including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Work_and_the_Glory" title="The Work and the Glory">
        The Work and the Glory
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Other_Side_of_Heaven" title="The Other Side of Heaven">
        The Other Side of Heaven
       </a>
      </i>
      have found acceptance both within and outside the church;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYU_TV" title="BYU TV">
       BYU TV
      </a>
      , the church-sponsored television station, also airs on several networks. The church also produces
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_pageants_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="List of pageants of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       six pageants
      </a>
      annually depicting various events of the primitive and modern-day church. Its
      <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Arizona_Easter_Pageant" title="Mesa Arizona Easter Pageant">
       Easter pageant
       <i>
        Jesus the Christ
       </i>
      </a>
      has been identified as the "largest annual outdoor Easter pageant in the world."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVT_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EVT-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_(cropped).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="2216" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg/600px-Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mtchoirandorchestra_ConferenceCenter_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Mormon_Tabernacle_Choir" title="Mormon Tabernacle Choir">
         Mormon Tabernacle Choir
        </a>
        has received a
        <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
         Grammy Award
        </a>
        , two
        <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">
         Emmy Awards
        </a>
        , two
        <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">
         Peabody Awards
        </a>
        , and the
        <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" title="National Medal of Arts">
         National Medal of Arts
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       No question the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints is "having a moment" ... The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Twilight_(series)" title="Twilight (series)">
         Twilight
        </a>
       </i>
       vampire novels of Mormon
       <a href="/wiki/Stephenie_Meyer" title="Stephenie Meyer">
        Stephenie Meyer
       </a>
       sell tens of millions of copies, Mormon convert
       <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Beck" title="Glenn Beck">
        Glenn Beck
       </a>
       inspires daily devotion and outrage with his radio show, and
       <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">
        HBO
       </a>
       generated lots of attention with the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Love" title="Big Love">
         Big Love
        </a>
       </i>
       finale. Even Broadway has gotten in on the act, giving us
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Mormon_(musical)" title="The Book of Mormon (musical)">
         The Book of Mormon
        </a>
       </i>
       , a big-budget musical about
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_missionaries" title="Mormon missionaries">
        Mormon missionaries
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">
        South Park
       </a>
       creators
       <a href="/wiki/Trey_Parker" title="Trey Parker">
        Trey Parker
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
        Matt Stone
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Avenue_Q" title="Avenue Q">
        Avenue Q
       </a>
       writer
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lopez" title="Robert Lopez">
        Robert Lopez
       </a>
       that, with 14 nominations, is expected to clean up at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Tony_Awards" title="2011 Tony Awards">
        (2011) Tony Awards
       </a>
       on June 12.|
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newsweek_magazine" title="Newsweek magazine">
         Newsweek magazine
        </a>
       </i>
       , June 2011
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsMorm_119-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NewsMorm-119">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         119
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Home_and_family">
       Home and family
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Home and family">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1995, the church's
      <a href="/wiki/First_Presidency_(LDS_Church)" title="First Presidency (LDS Church)">
       First Presidency
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve_(LDS_Church)" title="Quorum of the Twelve (LDS Church)">
       Quorum of the Twelve
      </a>
      issued "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Family:_A_Proclamation_to_the_World" title="The Family: A Proclamation to the World">
       The Family: A Proclamation to the World
      </a>
      ", which stresses the importance of the family. The proclamation states that "
      <a href="/wiki/Marriage_in_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Marriage in The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       marriage
      </a>
      between a man and a woman is ordained of God and that the family is central to the Creator's plan for the eternal destiny of His children." The document further says that "gender is an essential characteristic of individual premortal, mortal, and eternal identity and purpose," that the father and mother have differing but equal roles in raising children, and that successful marriages and families, founded upon the teachings of Jesus Christ, can last eternally.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This document is widely cited by LDS members as a statement of principle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The adult women (members of the church's
      <a href="/wiki/Relief_Society" title="Relief Society">
       Relief Society
      </a>
      ) in a congregation meet at least quarterly for additional instruction and service. The meetings may consist of a service project, conferences, or of various classes being offered.
     </p>
     <p>
      After interviewing and polling thousands of youth across America, evangelical statistician Christian Smith writes, "in general comparisons among major U.S. religious traditions using a variety of sociological measures of religious vitality and salience .... it is Mormon teenagers who are sociologically faring the best."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_events_and_gatherings">
       Social events and gatherings
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Social events and gatherings">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usapride_(cropped).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1911" data-file-width="3499" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg/450px-Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg/600px-Usapride_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Usapride_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        As part of its
        <a href="/wiki/Young_Men_(organization)" title="Young Men (organization)">
         Young Men program
        </a>
        , the church contributes more members to the
        <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">
         Boy Scouts of America
        </a>
        than any other
        <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America#Chartered_organizations_and_units" title="Boy Scouts of America">
         chartered organization
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
         <a href="#cite_note-130">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          130
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In addition to these regularly scheduled meetings, additional meetings are frequently held at the meetinghouse. Auxiliary officers may conduct leadership meetings or host training sessions and classes. The ward or branch community may schedule social activities at the meetinghouse, including dances, dinners, holiday parties and musical presentations. The church's
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Men_(organization)" title="Young Men (organization)">
       Young Men
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Women_(organization)" title="Young Women (organization)">
       Young Women
      </a>
      organizations meet at the meetinghouse once a week, where the youth participate in activities and work on
      <a href="/wiki/Duty_to_God_Award" title="Duty to God Award">
       Duty to God
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">
       Scouting
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_Progress" title="Personal Progress">
       Personal Progress
      </a>
      . Other popular activities are basketball, family history conferences, youth and singles conferences, dances, and various personal improvement classes. Church members may also reserve meetinghouses at no cost for weddings, receptions, and funerals.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the summer, the LDS Church hosts week-long seminars throughout North America known as Especially for Youth (EFY). This program is held Monday through Saturday during the summer months for youth ages 1418. During this week, youth often spend the night in college campus dorms and the day in various classes taught by adult religious educators, as well as participating in other various activities such as scripture study and dances.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_involvement">
       Political involvement
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Political involvement">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The LDS Church will take no partisan role in politics, stating that it will not "endorse, promote or oppose political parties, candidates or platforms; allow its church buildings, membership lists or other resources to be used for partisan political purposes; attempt to direct its members as to which candidate or party they should give their votes to ... or attempt to direct or dictate to a government leader."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PN_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PN-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While the church takes an apolitical approach to the candidates themselves, it encourages its members to play an active role as responsible citizens in their communities, including becoming informed about issues and voting in elections, and it actively works to counter anti-Mormonism that may come up during political campaigns. A 2012
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pew_Center" title="Pew Center">
       Pew Center
      </a>
      on Religion and Public Life survey indicates that 74 percent of U.S. members lean towards the
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican Party
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_News_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ABC_News-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some liberal members say they feel that they have to defend their worthiness due to political differences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-USA_Today-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Referring to the 2012 U.S Republican Presidential Primary,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Otterson" title="Michael Otterson">
       Michael Otterson
      </a>
      , the LDS Church's managing director for public affairs stated, "We now have two Latter-day Saints running, and the potential for misunderstanding or missteps is therefore twice what it was before."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj20110803_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wsj20110803-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the official church stance on staying out of politics does not include what church leaders deem to be moral issues. It has previously opposed same-sex marriage in
      <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8_(2008)#Religious_organizations" title="California Proposition 8 (2008)">
       California Prop 8
      </a>
      , supported a gay rights bill in Salt Lake City which bans discrimination against homosexual persons in housing and employment,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      opposed gambling, and supported the
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Compact" title="Utah Compact">
       Utah Compact
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In United States politics, there are 16 members of the church serving in the
      <a href="/wiki/114th_United_States_Congress" title="114th United States Congress">
       114th United States Congress
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
       Senate
      </a>
      Minority Leader,
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">
       Harry Reid
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDSList_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LDSList-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and one member serving as a
      <a href="/wiki/Governor_(United_States)" title="Governor (United States)">
       state governor
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Gary_Herbert" title="Gary Herbert">
       Gary Herbert
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Utah" title="Governor of Utah">
       Utah
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LDSList_139-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-LDSList-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Church member
      <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">
       Mitt Romney
      </a>
      was the
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican Party
      </a>
      's nominee in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">
       U.S. 2012 presidential election
      </a>
      and was defeated by incumbent U.S. President
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_Huntsman,_Jr." title="Jon Huntsman, Jr.">
       Jon Huntsman, Jr.
      </a>
      also sought the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_2012#Candidates" title="Republican Party (United States) presidential primaries, 2012">
       Republican nomination
      </a>
      until his withdrawal in early 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCMormon_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ABCMormon-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_services">
       Humanitarian services
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Humanitarian services">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2464" data-file-width="1632" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg/170px-USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg/255px-USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg/340px-USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USN_sailors_at_Beirut_pier_with_aid_cargo_Aug_4_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">
         U.S. Navy sailors
        </a>
        moving LDS Church-donated humanitarian supplies to
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beirut,_Lebanon" title="Beirut, Lebanon">
         Beirut, Lebanon
        </a>
        , in 2006
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Philanthropies" title="LDS Philanthropies">
       LDS Philanthropies
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Humanitarian_Services" title="LDS Humanitarian Services">
       LDS Humanitarian Services
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church is widely known for its worldwide
      <a href="/wiki/Humanitarianism" title="Humanitarianism">
       humanitarian services
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbs_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pbs-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philanthropy_142-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-philanthropy-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church's welfare and humanitarian efforts are coordinated by
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Philanthropies" title="LDS Philanthropies">
       LDS Philanthropies
      </a>
      (LDSP), a church department under the direction of the
      <a href="/wiki/Presiding_Bishop_(LDS_Church)" title="Presiding Bishop (LDS Church)">
       Presiding Bishopric
      </a>
      . Welfare efforts, originally initiated during the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , provide aid for the poor, financed by donations from church members. LDSP is also responsible for philanthropic donations to the LDS Church and other affiliated charities, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_History_Library" title="Church History Library">
       Church History Library
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_Educational_System" title="Church Educational System">
       Church Educational System
      </a>
      which includes
      <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">
       Brigham Young University
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_Education_Fund" title="Perpetual Education Fund">
       Perpetual Education Fund
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_Cultural_Center" title="Polynesian Cultural Center">
       Polynesian Cultural Center
      </a>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Mormon_Tabernacle_Choir" title="Mormon Tabernacle Choir">
       Mormon Tabernacle Choir
      </a>
      , and efforts dedicated to providing funds for
      <a href="/wiki/Missionary_(LDS_Church)" title="Missionary (LDS Church)">
       LDS missionaries
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_(LDS_Church)" title="Temple (LDS Church)">
       temple
      </a>
      construction.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
         <span title="The material in the vicinity of this tag may lack enough specific information to be verifiable (March 2014)">
          not specific enough to verify
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Donations are also used to operate
      <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_storehouse" title="Bishop's storehouse">
       bishop's storehouses
      </a>
      , which package and store food for the poor at low cost. Distribution of funds and food is administered by local
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_(LDS_Church)" title="Bishop (LDS Church)">
       bishops
      </a>
      . These local storehouses distribute commodities to the needy as requested by local bishops on a specified form. Bishop's storehouses also provide service opportunities for those receiving assistance and for those desiring to serve missions or to volunteer in the church's welfare program. The day-to-day operations of the storehouses are typically run by senior-aged missionaries as store managers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The church also distributes money through its
      <a href="/wiki/LDS_Humanitarian_Services" title="LDS Humanitarian Services">
       Humanitarian Services
      </a>
      division to natural disaster victims worldwide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church's Humanitarian Center, established in 1991, prepares emergency relief supplies for worldwide shipment to disaster victims, works to establish a global sense of self-reliance, and offers service opportunities to both church members and non-members. The emergency relief supplies that the church donates typically include clothing, personal care kits, and medical supplies. According to the LDS Humanitarian Center website, it ships about 12 million pounds of shoes and clothing, one million hygiene kits, and one million pounds of medical supplies per year, to relieve suffering in more than 100 countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When a disaster strikes, the church works with local government officials and other organizations to determine the immediate needs, and sends the necessary supplies and food to the affected area within hours. Missionaries are then sent to help alleviate other long-term damages by assisting injured persons and reconstructing damaged buildings. The church carries out these efforts without regard to the nationality or religion of the recipients, and 100 percent of the financial contributions donated to the church by members and non-members are used for humanitarian purposes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The church has been involved in providing relief aid for victims of several disasters in recent years, including
      <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
       Hurricane Katrina
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">
       2010 Haiti earthquake
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/2011_Christchurch_earthquake" title="2011 Christchurch earthquake">
       2011 Christchurch earthquake
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami">
       2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005 the church partnered with
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Relief_Services" title="Catholic Relief Services">
       Catholic Relief Services
      </a>
      to provide aid for struggling families and individuals in Niger,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and it has also partnered with
      <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Relief" title="Islamic Relief">
       Islamic Relief
      </a>
      to help victims of flooding in Pakistan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, the church sponsors five global projects (
      <a href="/wiki/Infant_respiratory_distress_syndrome" title="Infant respiratory distress syndrome">
       neonatal
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation" title="Cardiopulmonary resuscitation">
       resuscitation
      </a>
      training, clean water projects, wheelchair distribution, vision treatment, and
      <a href="/wiki/Measles_vaccine" title="Measles vaccine">
       measles vaccinations
      </a>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and works with local government agencies and other religious and secular organizations such as the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">
       American Red Cross
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">
       UNICEF
      </a>
      to accomplish these needs. In 2003 the church joined
      <a href="/wiki/Measles_Initiative" title="Measles Initiative">
       Measles Initiative
      </a>
      and has committed one million dollars per year to the campaign.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_and_criticism">
       Controversy and criticism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Controversy and criticism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="Criticism of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
       Criticism of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The LDS Church has been subject to criticism and sometimes
      <a href="/wiki/Anti-Mormonism" title="Anti-Mormonism">
       discrimination
      </a>
      since its early years in New York and
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
       Pennsylvania
      </a>
      . In the late1820s, criticism centered around the claim by Joseph Smith to have been led to a set of golden plates from which the Book of Mormon was reputedly translated.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1830s, the greatest criticism was for Smith's handling of a
      <a href="/wiki/Kirtland_Safety_Society" title="Kirtland Safety Society">
       banking failure
      </a>
      in Kirtland, Ohio, and the LDS Church's political and military power in Missouri, culminating in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_War_(1838)" title="Mormon War (1838)">
       1838 Mormon War
      </a>
      . In the 1840s, criticism of the church centered on its
      <a href="/wiki/Theodemocracy" title="Theodemocracy">
       theocratic
      </a>
      aspirations in Nauvoo, Illinois. Criticism of the practice of plural marriage and other doctrines taught by Smith appeared in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nauvoo_Expositor" title="Nauvoo Expositor">
        Nauvoo Expositor
       </a>
      </i>
      , which led to a series of events culminating in
      <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Joseph_Smith" title="Death of Joseph Smith">
       Smith's murder
      </a>
      in 1844.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prop8templeProtest.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2056" data-file-width="3088" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Prop8templeProtest.jpg/220px-Prop8templeProtest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Prop8templeProtest.jpg/330px-Prop8templeProtest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Prop8templeProtest.jpg/440px-Prop8templeProtest.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prop8templeProtest.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Protesters in front of the
        <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach_California_Temple" title="Newport Beach California Temple">
         Newport Beach California Temple
        </a>
        voicing their opposition to the church's support of
        <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8_(2008)" title="California Proposition 8 (2008)">
         Prop 8
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As the church began openly practicing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plural_marriage" title="Plural marriage">
       plural marriage
      </a>
