      under Brigham Young during the second half of the 19th century, the church became the target of nationwide criticism for that practice, as well as for the church's theocratic aspirations in the Utah Territory. Beginning in 1857, the church also came under
      <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Meadows_massacre_and_the_media" title="Mountain Meadows massacre and the media">
       significant media criticism
      </a>
      after the
      <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Meadows_massacre" title="Mountain Meadows massacre">
       Mountain Meadows massacre
      </a>
      in southern Utah.
     </p>
     <p>
      Academic critics have questioned the legitimacy of Smith as a prophet as well as the
      <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_Book_of_Mormon" title="Criticism of the Book of Mormon">
       historical authenticity of the Book of Mormon
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Abraham" title="Book of Abraham">
       Book of Abraham
      </a>
      . Criticism has expanded to include claims of historical revisionism, homophobia, racism, and sexist policies. Notable 20th-century critics include
      <a href="/wiki/Jerald_and_Sandra_Tanner" title="Jerald and Sandra Tanner">
       Jerald and Sandra Tanner
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fawn_Brodie" title="Fawn Brodie">
       Fawn Brodie
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Christians" title="Evangelical Christians">
       Evangelical Christians
      </a>
      continue to argue that Smith was either fraudulent or
      <a href="/wiki/Delusion" title="Delusion">
       delusional
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_apologetics" title="Mormon apologetics">
       Mormon apologetics
      </a>
      organizations, such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Apologetic_Information_%26_Research" title="Foundation for Apologetic Information &amp; Research">
       Foundation for Apologetic Information &amp; Research
      </a>
      (FAIR) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Ancient_Research_and_Mormon_Studies" title="Foundation for Ancient Research and Mormon Studies">
       Foundation for Ancient Research and Mormon Studies
      </a>
      (FARMS), have been founded to counter these criticisms. Most of the apologetic work focuses on providing and discussing evidence supporting the claims of Smith and the Book of Mormon, and much of it features criticism of the perceived lack of honesty when it comes to the scholarship of non-Mormon critics. Scholars and authors such as
      <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Nibley" title="Hugh Nibley">
       Hugh Nibley
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Daniel_C._Peterson" title="Daniel C. Peterson">
       Daniel C. Peterson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Lindsay_(engineer)" title="Jeff Lindsay (engineer)">
       Jeff Lindsay
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card" title="Orson Scott Card">
       Orson Scott Card
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/James_E._Talmage" title="James E. Talmage">
       James E. Talmage
      </a>
      are well-known apologists within the church.
     </p>
     <p>
      In recent years, the Internet has provided a new forum for proponents and critics of religions, including the LDS Church.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church's support in 2008 of California's
      <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8_(2008)" title="California Proposition 8 (2008)">
       Proposition 8
      </a>
      sparked heated debate and protest by gay-rights organizations and others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The church expressed support for a Salt Lake City ordinance protecting members of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_community" title="Gay community">
       LGBT community
      </a>
      against discrimination in employment and housing while allowing religious institutions to consider lifestyles in actions such as hiring or providing university accommodations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Jewish groups criticized the LDS Church in 1995 after discovering that vicarious
      <a href="/wiki/Baptism_for_the_dead" title="Baptism for the dead">
       baptisms for the dead
      </a>
      for victims of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
       Holocaust
      </a>
      had been performed by members of the church.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urbina_163-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urbina-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After that criticism, church leaders put a policy in place to stop the practice, with an exception for baptisms specifically requested or approved by victims' relatives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_LDS_Agreement_165-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_LDS_Agreement-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jewish organizations again criticized the church in 2002, 2004, 2008, and 2012
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      stating that the church failed to honor the 1995 agreement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_LDS_Agreement_165-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_LDS_Agreement-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The LDS Church says it has put institutional safeguards in place to avoid the submission of the names of Holocaust victims not related to Mormon members, but that the sheer number of names submitted makes policing the database of names impractical.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urbina_163-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urbina-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Due to doctrinal differences, the LDS Church is generally considered to be distinct and separate from mainstream Christianity by
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
       Catholic
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
       Protestant
      </a>
      churches, which express differences with one another but consider each other's churches as Christian.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many have accused the LDS Church of not being a Christian church at all as a result of disagreements with Apostolic succession and the "Great Apostasy", the
      <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">
       Nicene Creed
      </a>
      and, more so, Mormon cosmology and its plan of salvation including the doctrines of
      <a href="/wiki/Pre-existence#Mormonism" title="Pre-existence">
       pre-mortal life
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Baptism_for_the_dead" title="Baptism for the dead">
       baptism for the dead
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_glory" title="Degrees of glory">
       three degrees of heaven
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Mormonism)" title="Exaltation (Mormonism)">
       exaltation
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
       See also

     <p>
      <b>
       Notes
      </b>
     </p>
     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-THBJ-1">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-THBJ_1-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/manual/teachings-heber-j-grant/chapter-7" rel="nofollow">
           "Chapter 7: Personal, Abiding Testimony"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teachings_of_Presidents_of_the_Church:_Heber_J._Grant" title="Teachings of Presidents of the Church: Heber J. Grant">
            Teachings of Presidents of the Church: Heber J. Grant
           </a>
          </i>
          . Salt Lake City, Utah: LDS Church. 2011. pp.6270.
          <a class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20141208215734/https://www.lds.org/manual/teachings-heber-j-grant/chapter-7" rel="nofollow">
           Archived
          </a>
          from the original on 2014-12-08.
         </span>

           ^

        <span class="reference-text">
         "For salvation cometh to none such except it be through repentance and faith on the Lord Jesus Christ." Book of Mormon,
         <span class="plainlinks">
          <a class="external text" href="http://lds.org/scriptures/bofm/mosiah/3.12?lang=eng#11" rel="nofollow">

       <li id="cite_note-12">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-12">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFOaks2008">
          <a href="/wiki/Dallin_H._Oaks" title="Dallin H. Oaks">
           Oaks, Dallin H.
          </a>
          (May 2008),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/2008/05/testimony" rel="nofollow">
           "Testimony"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Ensign_(LDS_magazine)" title="Ensign (LDS magazine)">
            Ensign
           </a>
          </i>
          ,
          <q>
           Perhaps the puzzle some feel can be explained by the reality that each of us has two different channels to God. We have a channel of governance through our prophet and other leaders. This channel, which has to do with doctrine, ordinances, and commandments, results in obedience. We also have a channel of personal testimony, which is direct to God. This has to do with His existence, our relationship to Him, and the truth of His restored gospel. This channel results in knowledge.
          </q>
         </span>

       <li id="cite_note-15">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-15">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Scholars and eye-witnesses disagree whether the church was organized in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_(town),_New_York" title="Manchester (town), New York">
          Manchester, New York
         </a>
         at the Smith log home, or in
         <a href="/wiki/Fayette,_New_York" title="Fayette, New York">
          Fayette
         </a>
         at the home of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Whitmer" title="Peter Whitmer">
          Peter Whitmer
         </a>
         .
         <a href="#CITEREFBushman2005">
          Bushman 2005
         </a>
         , p.109;
         <a href="#CITEREFMarquardt2005">
          Marquardt 2005
         </a>
         , pp.22323 (arguing that organization in Manchester is most consistent with eye-witness statements). The LDS Church officially favors organization in Fayette.
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFLloyd2009">
          Lloyd, R. Scott (May 22, 2009),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.ldschurchnewsarchive.com/articles/57380/Major-discovery-discussed-at-Mormon-History-Association-Conference.html" rel="nofollow">

           </span>

          (LDS Church)

          </a>

       <li id="cite_note-38">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-38">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Many local Illinoisans were uneasy with Mormon power, and their unease was fanned by the local media after Smith suppressed a newspaper containing an expos regarding plural marriage, theocracy, and other sensitive and oft misinterpreted issues. The suppression resulted in Smith being arrested, tried, and acquitted for "inciting a riot". On June 25, Joseph let himself be arrested and tried for the riot charges again, this time in Carthage, the county seat, where he was incarcerated without bail on a new charge of treason.
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFBentley1992">
          <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I._Bentley" title="Joseph I. Bentley">
           Bentley, Joseph I.
          </a>
          (1992),
          <a class="external text" href="http://contentdm.lib.byu.edu/cdm/ref/collection/EoM/id/4208" rel="nofollow">
           "Smith, Joseph: Legal Trials of Joseph Smith"
          </a>
          , in
          <a href="/wiki/Daniel_H._Ludlow" title="Daniel H. Ludlow">
           Ludlow, Daniel H
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_Mormonism" title="Encyclopedia of Mormonism">
            Encyclopedia of Mormonism
           </a>
          </i>
          , New York:
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macmillan_Publishing" title="Macmillan Publishing">
           Macmillan Publishing
          </a>
          , pp.13461348,
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-02-879602-0" title="Special:BookSources/0-02-879602-0">

       <li id="cite_note-41">

       <li id="cite_note-42">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-42">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Smith's position as Prophet and
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Church" title="President of the Church">
          President of the Church
         </a>
         was originally left vacant, but later filled when the apostles could regroup based on the restored principle that the most senior apostle would always be the next President of the Church. As a result, Young, and any other senior
         <a href="/wiki/Apostle_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Apostle (Latter Day Saints)">
          apostle
         </a>
         of the
         <a href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve" title="Quorum of the Twelve">
          Quorum of the Twelve
         </a>
         , would be ordained
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Church_(LDS_Church)" title="President of the Church (LDS Church)">
          President of the Church
         </a>
         as a matter of course upon the death of the former President, subject to unanimous agreement of the Quorum of the Twelve.
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-44">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-44">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         In 2004, the State of Illinois recognized the expulsion of the Latter-day Saints as the "largest forced migration in American history" and stated in the adopted resolution that, "WHEREAS, The biases and prejudices of a less enlightened age in the history of the State of Illinois caused unmeasurable hardship and trauma for the community of Latter-day Saints by the distrust, violence, and inhospitable actions of a dark time in our past; therefore, be it resolved, by the House of Representatives of the Ninety-third General Assembly of the State of Illinois, that we acknowledge the disparity of those past actions and suspicions, regretting the expulsion of the community of Latter-day Saints, a people of faith and hard work."
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.ilga.gov/legislation/fulltext.asp?GAID=3&amp;SessionID=3&amp;GA=93&amp;DocTypeID=HR&amp;DocNum=0793&amp;LegID=12984&amp;SpecSess=&amp;Session=" rel="nofollow">
          "Official House Resolution HR0793 (LRB093 21726 KEF 49525 r), Illinois General Assembly, April 1, 2004
         </a>

       <li id="cite_note-47">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-47">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Mormon doctrine of plural wives was officially announced by one of the
         <a href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve" title="Quorum of the Twelve">
          Twelve Apostles
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Orson_Pratt" title="Orson Pratt">
          Orson Pratt
         </a>
         and Smith's successor
         <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">
          Brigham Young
         </a>
         in a special conference of the elders of the church assembled in the
         <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Tabernacle" title="Salt Lake Tabernacle">
          Salt Lake Tabernacle
         </a>
         on August 28, 1852, and reprinted in an extra edition of the
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Deseret_News" title="Deseret News">
           Deseret News
          </a>
         </i>
         Only a small percentage of church leaders participated in plural marriage believing it was a part of a restitution of ancient Priesthood blessings and a commandment of god to raise up a righteous generation. At the time, it was not barred by statute within the United States.
         <span class="citation news">
          "Minutes of conference: a special conference of the elders of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints assembled in the Tabernacle, Great Salt Lake City, August 28th, 1852, 10 o'clock, a.m., pursuant to public notice".
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Deseret_News" title="Deseret News">
            Deseret News Extra
           </a>
          </i>
          . September 14, 1852. p.14.
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Minutes+of+conference%3A+a+special+conference+of+the+elders+of+The+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints+assembled+in+the+Tabernacle%2C+Great+Salt+Lake+City%2C+August+28th%2C+1852%2C+10+o%27clock%2C+a.m.%2C+pursuant+to+public+notice&amp;rft.date=September+14%2C+1852&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Deseret+News+Extra&amp;rft.pages=14&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         . See also:
         <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_Latter_Day_Saint_polygamy#The_1850s:_Official_sanction_in_the_LDS_Church" title="Origin of Latter Day Saint polygamy">
          The 1850s: Official sanction in the LDS Church
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-48">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-48">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         See Tullidge, Edward,
         <i>
          History of Salt Lake City
         </i>
         , 132-35 (Original from the University of Michigan, 1886).
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-49">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-49">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The most notable instance of violence during this war was the tragic
         <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Meadows_massacre" title="Mountain Meadows massacre">
          Mountain Meadows massacre
         </a>
         , in which leaders of a local Mormon militia, contrary to top church leaders orders, ordered the massacre of a civilian emigrant party who had the misfortune of traveling through Utah during the escalating military tensions. The Mormons feared the mobs which murdered their families at the Haun's mill massacre and other illegal thefts of land, and murders which had plagued them back east.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-50">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-50">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         To combat the notion that rank-and-file Mormons were unhappy under Youngs leadership, Cumming noted that he had offered to help any leave the territory who desired. Of the 50,000 inhabitants of the territory of Utah, the underwhelming response56 men, 33 women, and 71 children, most of whom stated they left for economic reasonsimpressed Cumming, as did the fact that Mormon leaders contributed supplies to the emigrants. Cumming to [Secretary of State Lewis Cass], written by Thomas Kane, May 2, 1858, BYU Special Collections.
        </span>
       </li>

          <q>
           The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints teaches that all resurrected and perfected mortals become gods. [] Those who achieve this state of perfection will become joint-heirs with Christ. [] Latter-day Saints believe that those who become gods will have the opportunity to [] add[] further offspring to the eternal family.

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.aulast=LDS+Church&amp;rft.au=LDS+Church&amp;rft.btitle=Church+Handbook+of+Instructions%3A+Book+1%2C+Stake+Presidencies+and+Bishoprics&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=80&amp;rft.place=Salt+Lake+City%2C+Utah&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">

       <li id="cite_note-75">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-75">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         A man may be sealed to more than one wife if his previous wives are either dead or legally divorced from him; a living woman, however, may only be sealed to one husband. See
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFLDS_Church2006">
          LDS Church (2006),
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_Handbook_of_Instructions" title="Church Handbook of Instructions">
            Church Handbook of Instructions
           </a>
          </i>
          , Salt Lake City, Utah: LDS Church, p.85
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.aulast=LDS+Church&amp;rft.au=LDS+Church&amp;rft.btitle=Church+Handbook+of+Instructions&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=85&amp;rft.place=Salt+Lake+City%2C+Utah&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         . Thus, there is a common view within the LDS Church that though prohibited by the LDS Church in mortality,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plural_marriage" title="Plural marriage">
          plural marriage
         </a>
         will exist in the afterlife. See, e.g.,
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFPenrose1897">
          <a href="/wiki/Charles_W._Penrose" title="Charles W. Penrose">
           Penrose, Charles W.
          </a>
          (1897),
          <i>
           Mormon Doctrine Plain and Simple, or Leaves from the Tree of Life
          </i>
          , Salt Lake City, UT, p.66
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.aufirst=Charles+W.&amp;rft.aulast=Penrose&amp;rft.au=Penrose%2C+Charles+W.&amp;rft.btitle=Mormon+Doctrine+Plain+and+Simple%2C+or+Leaves+from+the+Tree+of+Life&amp;rft.date=1897&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=66&amp;rft.place=Salt+Lake+City%2C+UT&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         ("In the case of a man marrying a wife in the everlasting covenant who dies while he continues in the flesh and marries another by the same divine law, each wife will come forth in her order and enter with him into his glory.");
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFSmith1954.E2.80.9356">
          <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fielding_Smith" title="Joseph Fielding Smith">
           Smith, Joseph Fielding
          </a>
          (195456),
          <a href="/wiki/Bruce_R._McConkie" title="Bruce R. McConkie">
           McConkie, Bruce R.
          </a>
          , ed.,
          <i>
           Doctrines of Salvation: Sermons and Writings of Joseph Fielding Smith
          </i>
          <b>
           2
          </b>
          , Bookcraft, p.2
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.aufirst=Joseph+Fielding&amp;rft.aulast=Smith&amp;rft.au=Smith%2C+Joseph+Fielding&amp;rft.btitle=Doctrines+of+Salvation%3A+Sermons+and+Writings+of+Joseph+Fielding+Smith&amp;rft.date=1954-56&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=Bookcraft&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.volume=2">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         (stating of his deceased wives: "my wives will be mine forever").
        </span>

       <li id="cite_note-76">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-76">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         See
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFHyer1992">
          Hyer, Paul V. (1992), "Sealing: Temple Sealings", in Ludlow, Daniel H.,
          <a class="external text" href="http://contentdm.lib.byu.edu/u?/EoM,4177" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Encyclopedia of Mormonism
           </i>
          </a>
          , New York: Mcmillan, p.12891290,
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X">
           0-02-904040-X
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Sealing%3A+Temple+Sealings&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul+V.&amp;rft.au=Hyer%2C+Paul+V.&amp;rft.aulast=Hyer&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Mormonism&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcontentdm.lib.byu.edu%2Fu%3F%2FEoM%2C4177&amp;rft.isbn=0-02-904040-X&amp;rft.pages=12891290&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Mcmillan&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         ;
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFThomas1992">
          Thomas, Ryan L. (1992), "Adoption of Children", in Ludlow, Daniel H.,
          <a class="external text" href="http://contentdm.lib.byu.edu/u?/EoM,5451" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Encyclopedia of Mormonism
           </i>
          </a>
          , New York: Mcmillan, pp.2021,
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X">
           0-02-904040-X
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Adoption+of+Children&amp;rft.aufirst=Ryan+L.&amp;rft.aulast=Thomas&amp;rft.au=Thomas%2C+Ryan+L.&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Mormonism&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcontentdm.lib.byu.edu%2Fu%3F%2FEoM%2C5451&amp;rft.isbn=0-02-904040-X&amp;rft.pages=20-21&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Mcmillan&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         . Children born to biological parents who have been sealed to each other are considered "born in the covenant" and need not be sealed to their parents. See
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFCottrell1992">
          Cottrell, Ralph L. (1992), "Born in the Covenant", in Ludlow, Daniel H.,
          <a class="external text" href="http://contentdm.lib.byu.edu/u?/EoM,5557" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Encyclopedia of Mormonism
           </i>
          </a>
          , New York: Macmillan, p.218,
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-02-904040-X">
           0-02-904040-X
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Born+in+the+Covenant&amp;rft.au=Cottrell%2C+Ralph+L.&amp;rft.aufirst=Ralph+L.&amp;rft.aulast=Cottrell&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Mormonism&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcontentdm.lib.byu.edu%2Fu%3F%2FEoM%2C5557&amp;rft.isbn=0-02-904040-X&amp;rft.pages=218&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         .
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-wordofwisdom-77">

          Doctrine and Covenants
         </a>
         <span class="plainlinks">

       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-tithe-78">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-tithe_78-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation">
          <a class="external text" href="https://www.lds.org/topics/tithing?lang=eng" rel="nofollow">
           "Gospel Topics: Tithing"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           LDS.org
          </i>
          (LDS Church)
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Gospel+Topics%3A+Tithing&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Ftopics%2Ftithing%3Flang%3Deng&amp;rft.jtitle=LDS.org&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-fastoffering-79">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-fastoffering_79-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation">
          <a class="external text" href="https://www.lds.org/topics/fasting-and-fast-offerings?lang=eng" rel="nofollow">
           "Gospel Topics: Fasting and Fast Offerings"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           LDS.org
          </i>
          (LDS Church)
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Gospel+Topics%3A+Fasting+and+Fast+Offerings&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Ftopics%2Ffasting-and-fast-offerings%3Flang%3Deng&amp;rft.jtitle=LDS.org&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-80">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-80">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         In 1974, church president
         <a href="/wiki/Spencer_W._Kimball" title="Spencer W. Kimball">
          Spencer W. Kimball
         </a>
         said that "every male member of the Church should fill a mission".
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFKimball1974">
          <a href="/wiki/Spencer_W._Kimball" title="Spencer W. Kimball">
           Kimball, Spencer W.
          </a>
          (May 1974),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/1974/05/planning-for-a-full-and-abundant-life" rel="nofollow">
           "Planning for a Full and Abundant Life"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Ensign_(LDS_magazine)" title="Ensign (LDS magazine)">
            Ensign
           </a>
          </i>
          : 86,
          <q>
           The question is asked: Should every young man fill a mission? And the answer of the Church is yes, and the answer of the Lord is yes. Enlarging this answer we say: Certainly every male member of the Church should fill a mission, like he should pay his tithing, like he should attend his meetings, like he should keep his life clean and free from the ugliness of the world and plan a celestial marriage in the temple of the Lord. While there is no compulsion for him to do any of these things, he should do them for his own good.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Planning+for+a+Full+and+Abundant+Life&amp;rft.aufirst=Spencer+W.&amp;rft.au=Kimball%2C+Spencer+W.&amp;rft.aulast=Kimball&amp;rft.date=May+1974&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Fensign%2F1974%2F05%2Fplanning-for-a-full-and-abundant-life&amp;rft.jtitle=Ensign&amp;rft.pages=86&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         . The church's current president,
         <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">
          Thomas S. Monson
         </a>
         , stated in 2012 that "missionary work is a priesthood duty" and encouraged "all young men who are worthy and who are physically able and mentally capable to respond to the call to serve."
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFMonson2012">
          <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">
           Monson, Thomas S.
          </a>
          (November 2012),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/2012/11/welcome-to-conference" rel="nofollow">
           "Welcome to Conference"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           Ensign
          </i>
          ,
          <q>
           We affirm that missionary work is a priesthood dutyand we encourage all young men who are worthy and who are physically able and mentally capable to respond to the call to serve. Many young women also serve, but they are not under the same mandate to serve as are the young men. We assure the young sisters of the Church, however, that they make a valuable contribution as missionaries, and we welcome their service.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Welcome+to+Conference&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas+S.&amp;rft.aulast=Monson&amp;rft.au=Monson%2C+Thomas+S.&amp;rft.date=November+2012&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Fensign%2F2012%2F11%2Fwelcome-to-conference&amp;rft.jtitle=Ensign&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         In the church's October 2002 general conference,
         <a href="/wiki/M._Russell_Ballard" title="M. Russell Ballard">
          M. Russell Ballard
         </a>
         , of the
         <a href="/wiki/Quorum_of_the_Twelve_Apostles_(LDS_Church)" title="Quorum of the Twelve Apostles (LDS Church)">
          Quorum of the Twelve Apostles
         </a>
         , stated that local leaders recommend for full-time missions "only those young men ... whom you judge to be spiritually, physically, mentally, and emotionally prepared to face todays realities of missionary work"; he added that "not every young man needs to be called to serve away from his home; some may best serve under your direction as ward missionaries."
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFBallard2002">
          <a href="/wiki/M._Russell_Ballard" title="M. Russell Ballard">
           Ballard, M. Russell
          </a>
          (November 2002),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/2002/11/the-greatest-generation-of-missionaries" rel="nofollow">
           "The Greatest Generation of Missionaries"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Ensign_(LDS_magazine)" title="Ensign (LDS magazine)">
            Ensign
           </a>
          </i>
          ,
          <q>
           Upon you bishops and you stake presidents rests the responsibility to recommend only those young men and women whom you judge to be spiritually, physically, mentally, and emotionally prepared to face todays realities of missionary work. Brethren, judge wisely and remember: not every young man needs to be called to serve away from his home; some may best serve under your direction as ward missionaries.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=The+Greatest+Generation+of+Missionaries&amp;rft.au=Ballard%2C+M.+Russell&amp;rft.aufirst=M.+Russell&amp;rft.aulast=Ballard&amp;rft.date=November+2002&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Fensign%2F2002%2F11%2Fthe-greatest-generation-of-missionaries&amp;rft.jtitle=Ensign&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>

          <i>
           Ensign
          </i>
          : 71,
          <q>
           Then he taught and testified that even as Christ is risen from the dead, so will all men come forth from the grave; each will then be judged according to his works, and each will receive his appointed place in the mansions which are prepared. In that resurrected state, Paul said, there are 'celestial bodies, and bodies terrestrial, and bodies telestial; but the glory of the celestial, one; and the terrestrial, another; and the telestial, another' (JST, 1 Cor. 15:40)

        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-98">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The initial incorporation by the non-existent
         <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">
          State of Deseret
         </a>
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://content.lib.utah.edu/cdm4/document.php?CISOROOT=/uthisstat&amp;CISOPTR=1756&amp;REC=4" rel="nofollow">
           "(1851) Laws and Ordinances of the State of Deseret (Utah) Compilation 1851"
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.btitle=%281851%29+Laws+and+Ordinances+of+the+State+of+Deseret+%28Utah%29+Compilation+1851&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcontent.lib.utah.edu%2Fcdm4%2Fdocument.php%3FCISOROOT%3D%2Futhisstat%26CISOPTR%3D1756%26REC%3D4&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         was not legally valid, but was soon ratified by the
         <a href="/wiki/Utah_Territory" title="Utah Territory">
          Utah Territory
         </a>
         in 1851
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://content.lib.utah.edu/cdm4/document.php?CISOROOT=%2Futhisstat&amp;CISOPTR=448&amp;REC=3&amp;CISOBOX=Church+of+jesus+christ+of+latter-day+saints" rel="nofollow">
           "(1851) Acts Resolutions and Memorials Passed by the First Annual and Special Sessions of the Legislative Assembly of the Territory of Utah, 1851"
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.btitle=%281851%29+Acts+Resolutions+and+Memorials+Passed+by+the+First+Annual+and+Special+Sessions+of+the+Legislative+Assembly+of+the+Territory+of+Utah%2C+1851&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fcontent.lib.utah.edu%2Fcdm4%2Fdocument.php%3FCISOROOT%3D%252Futhisstat%26CISOPTR%3D448%26REC%3D3%26CISOBOX%3DChurch%2Bof%2Bjesus%2Bchrist%2Bof%2Blatter-day%2Bsaints&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         and 1855. See
         <i>
          Late Corporation of the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-Day Saints v. Romney
         </i>
         , 136 U.S. 4445 (1890).

       <li id="cite_note-104">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-104">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREF2013">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.mormonnewsroom.org/article/15-million-member-milestone-announced-at-churchs-general-conference" rel="nofollow">
           "News Release: 15 Million Member Milestone Announced at Church's General Conference"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           MormonNewsroom.org
          </i>
          (LDS Church), October 5, 2013
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=News+Release%3A+15+Million+Member+Milestone+Announced+at+Church%27s+General+Conference&amp;rft.date=October+5%2C+2013&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mormonnewsroom.org%2Farticle%2F15-million-member-milestone-announced-at-churchs-general-conference&amp;rft.jtitle=MormonNewsroom.org&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         ;
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFHales2009">
          Hales, Brook P. (May 2009),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/2009/05/statistical-report-2008" rel="nofollow">
           "Statistical Report, 2008"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           Ensign
          </i>
          : 30
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Statistical+Report%2C+2008&amp;rft.aufirst=Brook+P.&amp;rft.au=Hales%2C+Brook+P.&amp;rft.aulast=Hales&amp;rft.date=May+2009&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lds.org%2Fensign%2F2009%2F05%2Fstatistical-report-2008&amp;rft.jtitle=Ensign&amp;rft.pages=30&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         This is the church's own accounting, based on membership records. The church's definition of "membership" includes all persons who were ever baptized, or whose parents were members while the person was under the age of eight called "members of record" (
         <a href="#CITEREFLDS_Church2006">
          LDS Church 2006
         </a>
         , pp.14546), who have neither been excommunicated nor asked to have their names removed from church records (
         <a href="#CITEREFLDS_Church2006">
          LDS Church 2006
         </a>
         , pp.116, 14849).
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-105">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-105">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Subtracting U.S. membership of 6,144,582 (December 31, 2011) from total worldwide membership (December 31, 2011) of 14,441,346, results in 8,296,764 (rounded to 8.3 million) members outside the United States of America
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-114">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-114">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Relief_Society" title="Relief Society">
          Relief Society
         </a>
         was founded in 1842 in
         <a href="/wiki/Nauvoo,_Illinois" title="Nauvoo, Illinois">
          Nauvoo, Illinois
         </a>
         , and with the motto "Charity Never Faileth", the organization today includes more than 5 million women in more than 165 countries.
         <span class="citation">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.mormonnewsroom.org/article/relief-society-history" rel="nofollow">
           "Topic: Relief Society History"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           MormonNewsroom.org
          </i>
          (LDS Church)
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           , retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2014-09-23
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Church+of+Jesus+Christ+of+Latter-day+Saints&amp;rft.atitle=Topic%3A+Relief+Society+History&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mormonnewsroom.org%2Farticle%2Frelief-society-history&amp;rft.jtitle=MormonNewsroom.org&amp;rft.pub=LDS+Church&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         . Every Latter-day Saint woman age 18 or older is a member of the Relief Society.
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-122">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-122">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation" id="CITEREFCantwell2007">
          Cantwell, Robert W. (May 2007),
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lds.org/ensign/2007/05/church-auditing-department-report-2006" rel="nofollow">
           "Church Auditing Department Report, 2006"
          </a>
          ,
          <i>
           Ensign
          </i>
          ,
          <q>
           The Church Auditing Department has been granted access to all records and systems necessary to evaluate the adequacy of controls over receipts of funds, expenditures, and safeguarding of church assets. The Church Auditing Department is independent of all other church departments and operations, and the staff consists of certified public accountants, certified internal auditors, certified information systems auditors, and other credentialed professionals. Based upon audits performed, the Church Auditing Department is of the opinion that, in all material respects, contributions received, expenditures made, and assets of the church for the year 2006 have been recorded and administered in accordance with appropriate accounting practices, approved budgets, and church policies and procedures.
          </q>
         </span>
